#
# jeremy's calender
#
# 2007-10-10: convert german date format to iso and vice versa
# {:z}\.{:z}\.{:z} --> \3-\2-\1
# {:z}\-{:z}\-{:z} --> \3.\2.\1
#
# 2004: to print, i used ghostscript to convert
# to jpg, then inserted the jpg into word
# and scaled to 50% height, 40% width,
# where the calendar pages were lying on their left side,
# i.e. the heading (month name) was on the left-hand side
# of the page, then cut to 125 * 82 mm size.
#
# 2005: did the same, but printed on katja's
# canon bubblejet, and the pages turned out smaller.
#
opt -E                     # european dates
opt -F monday              # starting day of week
opt -m                     # draw a "moon" icon at full/new/quarter moons
opt -n Helvetica-Narrow/18 # notes font

#
# weekends with kids:
#
year 2003 # reset year explicitly
odd Sundays in year J
even Sundays in year K

year 2004 # reset year explicitly
odd Sundays in year J
even Sundays in year K

year 2005 # reset year explicitly
odd Sundays in year J
even Sundays in year K

year 2006 # reset year explicitly
odd Sundays in year J
even Sundays in year K

year 2007 # reset year explicitly
odd Sundays in year K
even Sundays in year J

year 2008 # reset year explicitly
odd Sundays in year K
even Sundays in year J

year 2009 # reset year explicitly
odd Sundays in year K
even Sundays in year J

# if your printer does not support AvantGarde)
#opt -d AvantGarde-Book/30 -t AvantGarde-Book -n Helvetica/8
#opt -d Helvetica-Bold/30 -t Helvetica-Bold -n Helvetica/8

#opt -s 0.6/0.97        # override default date/fill box shading
#ifndef whole_year
#  opt -O               # print outlined characters if "-w" NOT specified
#endif

#undef no_such_sym      # not an error to undef nonexistent symbol

#
# following entries apply to every year:
#
year *

# print week number each monday:
#
#all mondays in year w%u # first sunday defines week 1
all mondays in year w%w # first monday defines week 1

# continue silently if it does not:

#include? C:/j/doc/pcal/wg

good_friday*                    good friday
easter*                         easter sunday
mon after easter*               easter monday
last sunday in march            mother's day
last sunday in march            dst begins (+1h)
first day in may*               first of may
39th day after easter*          ascension day christi himmelfahrt
49th day after easter*          pentecost pfingsten # whitsun, the 50th day after easter sunday
1st monday after 49th day after easter*          whit monday pfingstmontag # first monday after whitsun
60th day after easter           corpus christi fronleichnam
3rd sunday in june              father's day
01 aug                          swiss national day
monday after 3rd sunday in september         ne jeune federal
03 oct                          german tag der einheit
last sunday in oct              dst ends (-1h)

2016-06-15 devcon@sf # Forge DevCon, Fort Mason, San Francisco, http://forge.autodesk.com/conference
2016-06-15 07:30-09:00 bim expert table
2016-06-15 11:00-12:00 manu@designden # Integrate and Extend Your Construction Ecosystem with BIM360 HQ APIs and Forge -- The BIM 360 web services simplify collaborative workflows from pre-construction through field management to handover of a construction project. In this session, we will discuss a new area of the BIM 360 API: HQ APIs for unified account administration and data across BIM 360. HQ APIs allow customers to integrate with BIM 360 and extend their construction eco-system to automate workflows, reduce manual data entry and improve data quality. The HQ API plays a critical role as part of the Forge platform, providing a secure and single point of integration for customer accounts, into their projects, partner companies, user management, and other account level information. We will introduce the basic functionalities of the HQ API and present use cases on how early adopters such as Layton Construction and JE Dunn Construction are leveraging this API to add value to their construction ecosystem. We will also share the latest developments and future direction for the BIM 360 product line and APIs,
2016-06-15 13:15-14:15 fernando@designden # Fernando Malard, OFCDesk: From Desktop to the Cloud with Forge -- This class will introduce the Forge platform from the perspective of an early adopter – starting with business aspects, paradigm shift, cloud concepts, and the future of Autodesk cloud platform strategy. We will cover some of the technical challenges with web programming from the perspective of someone migrating from a desktop programming environment to the cloud, and discuss how to overcome them. We will then walk through some simple yet representative code samples helping you to get started with the Forge platform through Model Derivative API and Design Automation services.
2016-06-15 14:25-15:25 philippe@designden # Visual Reporting with Connected Design Data -- Viewing a 3D model on a webpage or in a mobile app is really cool, but visualizing design data isn’t just about meshes and textures. In this class we will show you how the Forge Model Derivative API and JavaScript viewer give you access to the valuable data associated with each model component that is extracted from the original design file. We will take that a step further and connect those models to an external database to add even richer data. Finally, we will stylize the model to turn a model into a powerful, intuitive reporting tool.
2016-06-15 15:05-15:55 bim expert table
2016-06-15 16:00-21:30 3dwebfest # http://www.3dwebfest.com
2016-06-16 devcon@sf
2016-06-16 07:30-09:00 bim expert table
2016-06-16 13:00-14:00 free your bim data # room festival breakout 3
2016-06-16 15:35-16:35 anthony@festivalmain # The Future of Making Buildings: Forms Follow Formulae -- Computation can apply to far more than recording and communicating decisions about buildings through drawings. More than 50 years ago, advanced architecture and engineering firms foresaw the potential for technology to become an exploratory partner in the design and building process. Now this potential is being realized through the intersection of captured project intent, shared expertise, known physical and regulatory constraints, and scalable cloud computing. Autodesk is investing in this future, creating a platform to capture and express building expertise in the context of project requirements to rapidly arrive at possible solutions. This session will summarize three years of research and development in generative form and highlight current customer collaborations and coming development opportunities for the Autodesk partner network -- Anthony Hauck, Autodesk
2016-06-16 16:40-17:40 panel@festivalmain # Toward the Next Generation of BIM -- For the last decade, the building and construction industries have embraced the concept of BIM (Building Information Modeling) as the driver toward more unified, integrated modeling and processes. At the center of BIM is data that represents the building and process around it, and this data is becoming far more important than the tools that create it. Where is BIM heading next?  How the next generation of BIM is like? A panel of BIM experts will consider these questions from various perspectives: modeling tools, construction management, real world construction, and building owners and occupants; and discuss their latest work and ideas about future of BIM -- Kelly Cone, KP Reddy, Jim Awe, Manu Venugopal, Anthony Hauck
